        <title>Genome of extreme halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora | BMC Genomics | Full Text</title>

        

    <meta name="citation_abstract" content="Puccinellia tenuiflora, a forage grass, is considered a model halophyte given its strong tolerance for multiple stress conditions and its close genetic relationship with cereals. This halophyte has enormous values for improving our understanding of salinity tolerance mechanisms. The genetic information of P. tenuiflora also is a potential resource that can be used for improving the salinity tolerance of cereals. Here, we sequenced and assembled the P. tenuiflora genome (2n&#8201;=&#8201;14) through the combined strategy of Illumina, PacBio, and 10&#215; genomic technique. We generated 43.2&#215; PacBio long reads, 123.87&#215;&#8201;10&#215; genomic reads, and 312.6&#215; Illumina reads. Finally, we assembled 2638 scaffolds with a total size of 1.107 Gb, contig N50 of 117&#8201;kb, and scaffold N50 of 950&#8201;kb. We predicted 39,725 protein-coding genes, and identified 692 tRNAs, 68 rRNAs, 702 snRNAs, 1376 microRNAs, and 691&#8201;Mb transposable elements. We deposited the genome sequence in NCBI and the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center. Our work may improve current understanding of plant salinity tolerance, and provides extensive genetic resources necessary for improving the salinity and drought tolerance of cereals."/>

    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

    })();

    <link rel="canonical" href="//bmcgenomics.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5"/>
    

        
        
        
        <meta property="og:url" content="https://bmcgenomics.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5"/>
        <meta property="og:type" content="article"/>
        <meta property="og:site_name" content="BMC Genomics"/>
        <meta property="og:title" content="Genome of extreme halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora"/>
        <meta property="og:description" content="Puccinellia tenuiflora, a forage grass, is considered a model halophyte given its strong tolerance for multiple stress conditions and its close genetic relationship with cereals. This halophyte has enormous values for improving our understanding of salinity tolerance mechanisms. The genetic information of P. tenuiflora also is a potential resource that can be used for improving the salinity tolerance of cereals. Here, we sequenced and assembled the P. tenuiflora genome (2n&#x3D;14) through the combined strategy of Illumina, PacBio, and 10 genomic technique. We generated 43.2 PacBio long reads, 123.8710 genomic reads, and 312.6 Illumina reads. Finally, we assembled 2638 scaffolds with a total size of 1.107 Gb, contig N50 of 117kb, and scaffold N50 of 950kb. We predicted 39,725 protein-coding genes, and identified 692 tRNAs, 68 rRNAs, 702 snRNAs, 1376 microRNAs, and 691Mb transposable elements. We deposited the genome sequence in NCBI and the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center. Our work may improve current understanding of plant salinity tolerance, and provides extensive genetic resources necessary for improving the salinity and drought tolerance of cereals."/>

                        <h1 class="c-article-title" data-test="article-title" data-article-title="" itemprop="name headline">Genome of extreme halophyte <i>Puccinellia tenuiflora</i></h1>
                        <ul class="c-author-list js-etal-collapsed" data-etal="25" data-etal-small="3" data-test="authors-list" data-component-authors-activator="authors-list"><li             <a class="js-orcid" itemprop="url" href="http://orcid.org/0000-0002-3500-4808"><span class="u-visually-hidden">ORCID: </span>orcid.org/0000-0002-3500-4808</a></span><sup class="u-js-hide"><a href="#Aff2">2</a><span itemprop="affiliation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Organization" class="u-visually-hidden"><meta itemprop="name" content="Northeast Normal University" /><meta itemprop="address" content="0000 0004 1789 9163, grid.27446.33, Key laboratory of Molecular Epigenetics of Ministry of Education (MOE), Northeast Normal University, Changchun, 130024, China" /></span></sup></li></ul>
                        <p class="c-article-info-details" data-container-section="info">
                            
    <a data-test="journal-link" href="/"><i data-test="journal-title">BMC Genomics</i></a>

                            <b data-test="journal-volume"><span class="u-visually-hidden">volume</span>21</b>, Articlenumber:<span data-test="article-number">311</span> (<span data-test="article-publication-year">2020</span>)
            <a href="#citeas" class="c-article-info-details__cite-as u-hide-print" data-track="click" data-track-action="cite this article" data-track-label="link">Cite this article</a>
                        </p>

                    <p class="c-article-metrics-bar__count">882 <span class="c-article-metrics-bar__label">Accesses</span></p>
                </li>
            
            
            
            <li class="c-article-metrics-bar__item">
                <p class="c-article-metrics-bar__details"><a href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/metrics" data-track="click" data-track-action="view metrics" data-track-label="link" rel="nofollow">Metrics <span class="u-visually-hidden">details</span></a></p>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Background</h3><p><i>Puccinellia tenuiflora</i>, a forage grass, is considered a model halophyte given its strong tolerance for multiple stress conditions and its close genetic relationship with cereals. This halophyte has enormous values for improving our understanding of salinity tolerance mechanisms. The genetic information of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> also is a potential resource that can be used for improving the salinity tolerance of cereals.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Results</h3><p>Here, we sequenced and assembled the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome (2n=14) through the combined strategy of Illumina, PacBio, and 10 genomic technique. We generated 43.2 PacBio long reads, 123.8710 genomic reads, and 312.6 Illumina reads. Finally, we assembled 2638 scaffolds with a total size of 1.107 Gb, contig N50 of 117kb, and scaffold N50 of 950kb. We predicted 39,725 protein-coding genes, and identified 692 tRNAs, 68 rRNAs, 702 snRNAs, 1376 microRNAs, and 691Mb transposable elements.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Conclusions</h3><p>We deposited the genome sequence in NCBI and the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center. Our work may improve current understanding of plant salinity tolerance, and provides extensive genetic resources necessary for improving the salinity and drought tolerance of cereals.</p></div></div></section>
                    
    


                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Background"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Background</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Salinity stress affects over 6% of the global land area and is a severe problem that limits agriculture [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Flowers TJ, Yeo AR. Breeding for salinity resistance in crop plants: where next. Aust J Plant Physiol. 1995;22(6):87584." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d52386e521">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Flowers TJ, Galal HK, Bromham L. Evolution of halophytes: multiple origins of salt tolerance in land plants. Funct Plant Biol. 2010;37(7):60412." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d52386e524">2</a>]. Halophytes are remarkable plants that tolerate high salinity that would kill 99% of other plant species (glycophyte), and are applied to improve saline soil [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Yan XF, Sun GR. Physiological Ecology Research of Puccinellia tenuiflora. Beijing: Science Press; 2000 p. 200." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d52386e527">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Flowers TJ, Colmer TD. Salinity tolerance in halophytes. New Phytol. 2008;179(4):94563." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d52386e530">4</a>]. Some extreme halophytes can survive salinity levels &gt;1000mM NaCl, whereas glycophytes, such as rice and <i>Arabidopsis</i>, can only survive 50100mM NaCl [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Flowers TJ, Colmer TD. Salinity tolerance in halophytes. New Phytol. 2008;179(4):94563." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d52386e537">4</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Munns R, Tester M. Mechanisms of salinity tolerance. Annu Rev Plant Biol. 2008;59(1):65181." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d52386e540">5</a>]. Most botanists believe that these salt-sensitive glycophytes may provide limited insights into mechanisms of salinity tolerance, and that extreme halophytes may have enormous values for improving our understanding of salinity tolerance mechanisms [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Flowers TJ, Colmer TD. Salinity tolerance in halophytes. New Phytol. 2008;179(4):94563." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d52386e543">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Munns R, Tester M. Mechanisms of salinity tolerance. Annu Rev Plant Biol. 2008;59(1):65181." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d52386e543_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Flowers TJ. Physiology of halophytes. Plant Soil. 1985;89(13):4156." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d52386e546">6</a>]. Given that many important crops are gramineous, understanding the salinity tolerance mechanisms of gramineous halophytes will be helpful in improving the salinity or drought tolerance of cereal crops. Although the genomes of several salinity-tolerant plant species have been reported [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wu HJ, Zhang Z, Wang JY, Oh DH, Dassanayake M, Liu B, et al. Insights into salt tolerance from the genome of Thellungiella salsuginea. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2012;109(30):1221924." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d52386e549">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ma T, Wang J, Zhou G, Yue Z, Hu Q, Chen Y, et al. Genomic insights into salt adaptation in a desert poplar. Nat Commun. 2013;4(1):3797." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d52386e549_1">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Guo L, Qiu J, Ye C, Jin G, Mao L, Zhang H, et al. Echinochloa crus-galli genome analysis provides insight into its adaptation and invasiveness as a weed. Nat Commun. 2017;8(1):1031." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d52386e549_2">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Wang L, Ma G, Wang H, Chen C, Mu S, Wei Q, et al. A draft genome assembly of halophyte Suaeda aralocaspica, a plant that performs C4 photosynthesis within individual cells. GigaSci. 2019;8(9):giz116." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d52386e552">10</a>], the genome of an extreme Gramineae halophyte is unavailable. <i>Puccinellia tenuiflora</i> (2<i>n</i>=14) is a perennial halophyte of the Gramineae and is distributed in Asian and European grasslands [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Yan XF, Sun GR. Physiological Ecology Research of Puccinellia tenuiflora. Beijing: Science Press; 2000 p. 200." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d52386e562">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Zhao K, Song J, Feng G, Zhao M, Liu J. Species, types, distribution, and economic potential of halophytes in China. Plant Soil. 2011;342(12):495509." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d52386e565">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Meng X, Zhao Q, Jin Y, Yu J, Yin Z, Chen S, et al. Chilling-responsive mechanisms in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings revealed from proteomics analysis. J Proteome. 2016;143:36581." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52386e568">12</a>]. It is a forage grass with high nutritional value and strong tolerance for multiple stress conditions, such as drought, disease, and chilling [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Yan XF, Sun GR. Physiological Ecology Research of Puccinellia tenuiflora. Beijing: Science Press; 2000 p. 200." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d52386e571">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Zhao K, Song J, Feng G, Zhao M, Liu J. Species, types, distribution, and economic potential of halophytes in China. Plant Soil. 2011;342(12):495509." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d52386e575">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Meng X, Zhao Q, Jin Y, Yu J, Yin Z, Chen S, et al. Chilling-responsive mechanisms in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings revealed from proteomics analysis. J Proteome. 2016;143:36581." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52386e578">12</a>]. <i>P. tenuiflora</i> can survive at pH10 and 900mM NaCl [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Yan XF, Sun GR. Physiological Ecology Research of Puccinellia tenuiflora. Beijing: Science Press; 2000 p. 200." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d52386e584">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao K, Song J, Feng G, Zhao M, Liu J. Species, types, distribution, and economic potential of halophytes in China. Plant Soil. 2011;342(12):495509." href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d52386e587">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Meng X, Zhao Q, Jin Y, Yu J, Yin Z, Chen S, et al. Chilling-responsive mechanisms in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings revealed from proteomics analysis. J Proteome. 2016;143:36581." href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52386e587_1">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang X, Sun G, Wang J, Cao W, Liang J, Yu Z, et al. Relationships among MDA content, plasma membrane permeability and the chlorophyll fluorescence parameters of Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings under NaCl stress. Acta Ecol Sin. 2006;26(1):1229." href="#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d52386e587_2">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Xu A. Application of Puccinellia chinampoensis and Puccinellia tenuiflora in Western Jilin Province of China. China Grassl. 1990;2:625." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d52386e590">14</a>] and can grow normally and produce seeds under some extreme soil conditions (23% salt content and pH&gt;10) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Xu A. Application of Puccinellia chinampoensis and Puccinellia tenuiflora in Western Jilin Province of China. China Grassl. 1990;2:625." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d52386e594">14</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Xu H, Bao C, Ge C, Zhang P, Li L. Comparative study for two salt-tolerant herbages Puccinellia tenuiflora and Puccinellia chinampoensis. China Grassl. 1995;14:437." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d52386e597">15</a>]. Given these qualities, <i>P. tenuiflora</i> has been used to recover and exploit saline grasslands or croplands in northern China [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Xu A. Application of Puccinellia chinampoensis and Puccinellia tenuiflora in Western Jilin Province of China. China Grassl. 1990;2:625." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d52386e603">14</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Xu H, Bao C, Ge C, Zhang P, Li L. Comparative study for two salt-tolerant herbages Puccinellia tenuiflora and Puccinellia chinampoensis. China Grassl. 1995;14:437." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d52386e606">15</a>]. A growing number of molecular studies have focused on <i>P. tenuiflora</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Meng X, Zhao Q, Jin Y, Yu J, Yin Z, Chen S, et al. Chilling-responsive mechanisms in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings revealed from proteomics analysis. J Proteome. 2016;143:36581." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52386e613">12</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang YC, Yang CP, Liu GF, Jiang J. Development of a cDNA microarray to identify gene expression of Puccinellia tenuiflora under saline-alkali stress. Plant Physiol Biochem. 2007;45(8):56776." href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang Y, Chu Y, Liu G, Wang MH, Jiang J, Hou Y, et al. Identification of expressed sequence tags in an alkali grass (Puccinellia tenuiflora) cDNA library. J Plant Physiol. 2007;164(1):7889." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu H, Zhang XX, Takano T, Liu SK. Characterization of a PutCAX1 gene from Puccinellia tenuiflora that confers Ca2+ and Ba2+ tolerance in yeast. Biochem Biophys Res Commun. 2009;383(4):3926." href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_2">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Xie L, Takahashi R, Liu SK, Takano T. Cloning of a high-affinity K+ transporter gene PutHKT2;1 from Puccinellia tenuiflora and its functional comparison with OsHKT2; 1 from rice in yeast and Arabidopsis. J Exp Bot. 2009;60(12):3491502." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_3">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Liu SK, Takano T. Expression of the AKT1-type K+ channel gene from Puccinellia tenuiflora, PutAKT1, enhances salt tolerance in Arabidopsis. Plant Cell Rep. 2010;29(8):86574." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_4">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Nishiuchi S, Liu SK, Takano T. Ectopic expression of the channel  subunits from Puccinellia tenuiflora (KPutB1) and rice (KOB1) alters K+/Na+ homeostasis of yeast and Arabidopsis. Mol Biotechnol. 2011;48(1):7686." href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_5">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yu JJ, Chen SX, Zhao Q, Wang T, Yang CP, Diaz C, et al. Physiological and proteomic analysis of salinity tolerance in Puccinellia tenuiflora. J Proteome Res. 2011;10(9):385270." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_6">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang X, Wei L, Wang Z, Wang T. Physiological and molecular features of Puccinellia tenuiflora tolerating salt and alkaline-salt stress. J Integr Plant Biol. 2013;55(3):26276." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_7">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yu JJ, Chen SX, Wang T, Sun GR, Dai SJ. Comparative proteomic analysis of Puccinellia tenuiflora leaves under Na2CO3 stress. Int J Mol Sci. 2013;14(1):174062." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_8">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang P, Cui YN, Gao L, Wang SM. Construction of RNAi expression vector of CYP86A gene in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora. Acta Pratacul Sin. 2017;26(6):10510." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_9">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang WD, Wang P, Bao Z, Ma Q, Duan LJ, Bao AK, et al. SOS1, HKT1;5, and NHX1 synergistically modulate Na+ homeostasis in the halophytic grass Puccinellia tenuiflora. Front Plant Sci. 2017;8:576." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_10">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ye X, Wang H, Cao X, Jin X, Cui F, Bu Y, et al. Transcriptome profiling of Puccinellia tenuiflora during seed germination under a long-term saline-alkali stress. BMC Genomics. 2019;20(1):589." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d52386e616_11">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Yin Z, Zhang H, Zhao Q, Yoo M-J, Zhu N, Yu J, et al. Physiological and comparative proteomic analyses of saline-alkali NaHCO3-responses in leaves of halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora. Plant Soil. 2019;437(12):13758." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d52386e619">28</a>]. Currently, <i>P. tenuiflora</i> is recognized as a model halophyte [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Yan XF, Sun GR. Physiological Ecology Research of Puccinellia tenuiflora. Beijing: Science Press; 2000 p. 200." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d52386e625">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Meng X, Zhao Q, Jin Y, Yu J, Yin Z, Chen S, et al. Chilling-responsive mechanisms in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings revealed from proteomics analysis. J Proteome. 2016;143:36581." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52386e628">12</a>]. Unfortunately, the genomic sequence of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> is unavailable. Here, we provide first report on the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome. Our work may provide extensive genetic resources for improving the salinity or drought tolerance of cereals.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec2">Construction and content</h3><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec3">Evaluation of genome size</h4><p>Taxonomy characteristics of <i>Puccinellia tenuiflora</i> are available at Flora of China (<a href="http://www.efloras.org/florataxon.aspx?flora_id=2&amp;taxon_id=200026128">http://www.efloras.org/florataxon.aspx?flora_id=2&amp;taxon_id=200026128</a>). We surveyed the chromosome number of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> according to Kato et al. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Kato A, Lamb JC, Birchler JA, Wessler SR. Chromosome painting using repetitive DNA sequences as probes for somatic chromosome identification in maize. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2004;101(37):135549." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d52386e659">29</a>]. Total genomic DNA was extracted from fresh leaves. We used the conventional method to estimate the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome size. Briefly, we generated 49 Gb of high-quality short-insert Illumina reads to analyze the <i>K</i>-mer frequency of distribution [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Li R, Fan W, Tian G, Zhu H, He L, Cai J, et al. The sequence and de novo assembly of the giant panda genome. Nature. 2010;463(7279):3117." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d52386e669">30</a>]. Genome size was calculated using the following formula: Genome size=total <i>K</i>-mer number /<i>K</i>-mer depth [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Li R, Fan W, Tian G, Zhu H, He L, Cai J, et al. The sequence and de novo assembly of the giant panda genome. Nature. 2010;463(7279):3117." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d52386e678">30</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Kim EB, Fang X, Fushan AA, Huang Z, Lobanov AV, Han L, et al. Genome sequencing reveals insights into physiology and longevity of the naked mole rat. Nature. 2011;479(7372):2237." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d52386e681">31</a>], in which <i>K</i>-mer depth is the peak value of <i>K</i>-mer distribution. The chromosome number of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> is 14 (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Fig1">1</a>). Our <i>K</i>-mer analysis showed that the genome size of extreme halophyte <i>P. tenuiflora</i> was 1.303 Gb (2n=14) and the genome was complex, with 1.56% heterozygosity and 65.5% repeat content (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab1">1</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1186%2Fs12864-020-6727-5/MediaObjects/12864_2020_6727_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1186%2Fs12864-020-6727-5/MediaObjects/12864_2020_6727_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="1310" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>Chromosome number (<b>a</b>) and habitat (<b>b</b>) of <i>P. tenuiflora</i></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
<div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Results of <i>K-mer</i> analysis. The <i>K-mer</i> was defined as 17bp to assess <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome size by the following formula: total <i>K-mer</i> number/<i>K-mer</i> depth. The heterozygous ratio was determined by the number of heterozygous <i>K-mer/</i>total <i>K-mer</i> number</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Genome sequencing</h3><p>Illumina paired-end (PE) libraries were constructed with short insert sizes of 250 and 450bp. Illumina mate-pair (MP) libraries were constructed with insert sizes of 2, 5, and 10kbp (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab2">2</a>). We generated 209.13 Gb of raw data by the PE libraries, and 197.38 Gb of raw data by the MP libraries. The Illumina libraries were sequenced on Illumina HiSeq XTen platform. We also sequenced 56.12 Gb of PacBio long reads and 161.03 Gb of 10 genomics barcoded reads (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab2">2</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 Raw data of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> sequencing</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Genome assembly</h3><p>Because the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome is highly complex and repeated, its genome was assembled by a combined strategy of PacBio (third-generation), 10 genomic technique, and Illumina Hiseq (second-generation). We generated 312.6 reads of Illumina, 43.2 read of PacBio and 123.87 reads of 10 genomic. First the PacBio sequences were corrected for errors. The accurate sequences of PacBio were assembled into primary contigs based on FALCON (Branch 3.1) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Chin C-S, Peluso P, Sedlazeck FJ, Nattestad M, Concepcion GT, Clum A, et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single molecule real-time sequencing. Nat Methods. 2016;13(12):10504." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d52386e914">32</a>] and FALCON-Unzip software (<a href="https://github.com/PacificBiosciences/FALCON_unzip">https://github.com/PacificBiosciences/FALCON_unzip</a>). After treatment with FALCON-Unzip software, we corrected errors of these contigs using PacBio sequences based on quiver software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Chin C-S, Alexander DH, Marks P, Klammer AA, Drake J, Heiner C, et al. Nonhybrid, finished microbial genome assemblies from longread SMRT sequencing data. Nat Methods. 2013;10(6):5639." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d52386e921">33</a>] and using Illumina data based on pilon software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Walker BJ, Abeel T, Shea T, Priest M, Abouelliel A, Sakthikumar S, et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS One. 2014;9(11):e112963." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d52386e924">34</a>], and finally obtaining consensus sequences of high quality. Next, we used Illumina long reads of 2, 5, and 10kb to elongate and combine the preassembled contigs into scaffolds based on SSPACE software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Boetzer M, Henkel CV, Jansen HJ, Butler D, Pirovano W. Scaffolding pre-assembled contigs using SSPACE. Bioinformatics. 2011;27(4):5789." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d52386e928">35</a>], and then used 10 genomics linked-reads to further elongate and combine the scaffolds based on 10 FragScaff software. Lastly, we used Purge Haplotigs software (<a href="https://bitbucket.org/mroachawri/purge_haplotigs/overview">https://bitbucket.org/mroachawri/purge_haplotigs/overview</a>) to filter the redundant sequences caused by high heterozygosity. Finally, we assembled 2638 scaffolds with a total size of 1.107 Gb, contig N50 of 117kb, and scaffold N50 of 950kb (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab3">3</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-3"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab3" data-test="table-caption">Table 3 Assembly results of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/3"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Genome annotation</h3><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Annotation of replicate sequences</h3><p>Transposable elements (TEs) of the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome were annotated. We used two methods to find the TEs. The first method was RepeatMasker (version 3.3.0) to discover TEs in an integrated known replicate sequence library (Repbase 15.02) and the de novo replicate sequence library constructed by RepeatModeler (Version 1.0.5) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Smit AFA, Hubley R. RepeatModeler Open-1.0. 2008-2015. &#xA;http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;&#xA;. Accessed 1 Feb 2015." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1076">36</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Chen N. Using RepeatMasker to identify repetitive elements in genomic sequences. Curr Protoc Bioinformatics. 2009. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1002/0471250953.bi0410s25&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1079">37</a>], RepeatScout [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Price AL, Jones NC, Pevzner PA. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics. 2005;21(1):i3518." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1082">38</a>], and LTR_FINDER [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Xu Z, Wang H. LTR-FINDER: An efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 2007;35(2_1):W2658." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1085">39</a>]. The second method detected TEs in the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome using RepeatProteinMask by searching against the TE protein database [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Chen N. Using RepeatMasker to identify repetitive elements in genomic sequences. Curr Protoc Bioinformatics. 2009. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1002/0471250953.bi0410s25&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1092">37</a>]. We identified 691Mb transposable elements (62.44% of the total sequence), including 580Mb of LTR retrotransposons (52.43%) (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab4">4</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-4"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab4" data-test="table-caption">Table 4 Overview of the annotation of the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/4"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Annotation of protein-coding genes</h3><p>A combined strategy (de novo-, homolog-, and RNA-seq-based predictions) was used to annotate protein-coding genes in the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome using the following software: Augustus (version 3.0.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Stanke M, Waack S. Gene prediction with a hidden Markov model and a new intron submodel. Bioinformatics. 2003;19(2):ii21525." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1268">40</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Stanke M, Schoffmann O, Morgenstern B, Waack S. Gene prediction in eukaryotes with a generalized hidden Markov model that uses hints from external sources. BMC Bioinform. 2006;7(1):62." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1271">41</a>], Genescan (version 1.0) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Salamov AA, Solovyev VV. Ab initio gene finding in Drosophila genomic DNA. Genome Res. 2000;10(4):51622." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1274">42</a>], Geneid [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Parra G, Blanco E, Guigo R. GeneID in Drosophila. Genome Res. 2000;10(4):5115." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1277">43</a>], GlimmerHMM (version 3.0.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Majoros WH, Pertea M, Salzberg SL. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open-source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics. 2004;20(16):28789." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1281">44</a>], and SNAP [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Korf I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinform. 2004;5(1):59." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1284">45</a>]. The homologous sequences of six species (<i>Zea mays</i>, <i>Sorghum bicolor</i>, <i>Brachypodium distachyon</i>, <i>Setaria italica</i>, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>, and <i>Oryza sativa</i>) were aligned against the repeat-masked <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome with TBLASTN (E-value 105) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Altschul SF, Madden TL, Schffer AA, Zhang J, Zhang Z, Miller W, et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 1997;25(17):3389402." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1309">46</a>], and then Genewise software 2.2.0 was used to predict the gene models [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Birney E, Clamp M, Durbin R. Genewise and genomewise. Genome Res. 2004;14(5):98895." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1312">47</a>]. Two strategies were used to assemble the RNA-seq reads to the unique transcripts. First, we mapped the RNA-seq reads to the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome with Tophat 2.0.8 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Trapnell C, Pachter L, Salzberg SL. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics. 2009;25(9):110511." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1319">48</a>] and Cufflinks 2.1.1 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Trapnell C, Williams BA, Pertea G, Mortazavi A, Kwan G, van Baren MJ, et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat Biotechnol. 2010;28(5):5115." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1322">49</a>] (<a href="http://cufflinks.cbcb.umd.edu/">http://cufflinks.cbcb.umd.edu/</a>). Afterward, we used Trinity [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Grabherr MG, Haas BJ, Yassour M, Levin JZ, Thompson DA, Amit I, et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat Biotechnol. 2011;29(7):64452." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1329">50</a>] to assemble the RNA-seq reads, and then used PASA [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Haas BJ, Delcher AL, Mount SM, Wortman JR, Smith RK, Hannick LI, et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 2003;31(19):565466." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1332">51</a>] (<a href="http://pasapipeline.github.io/">http://pasapipeline.github.io/</a>) to improve the structure of the assembled genes. We generated non-redundant gene sets using EVidenceModeler (EVM) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Haas BJ, Salzberg SL, Zhu W, Pertea M, Allen JE, Orvis J, et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using evidence modeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 2008;9(1):R7." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1340">52</a>] via integrating gene prediction results of all methods. Finally, the predicted genes were filtered by three criteria: coding region length of 50 amino acids; FPKM &lt;5; and supported only by de novo strategy. Functions of the protein-coding genes were annotated by BLASTP program (best hit with E-value 1E-05) against three public protein databases: TrEMBL [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Bairoch A, Apweiler R. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 2000;28(1):458." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1343">53</a>], Swiss-Prot, and NR. The protein domains were analyzed by InterProScan software (4.8) via searching against InterPro databases 29.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Mulder N, Apweiler R. InterPro and InterProScan: tools for protein sequence classification and comparison. Methods Mol Biol. 2007;396(2):5970." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1346">54</a>], and the GO term information was collected from the InterPro annotation results [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Ashburner M, Ball CA, Blake JA, Botstein D, Butler H, Cherry JM, et al. Gene ontology: tool for the unification of biology. Nat Genet. 2000;25(1):259." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1349">55</a>]. Moreover, we also conducted KEGG annotation for all genes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Kanehisa M, Goto S. KEGG: Kyoto encyclopedia of genes and genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 2000;28(1):2730." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1352">56</a>].</p><p>On the basis of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genomic sequences, we predicted 39,725 protein-coding genes (Tables<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab5">5</a>). Of the 39,725 predicted protein-coding genes, the protein sequences of 39,470 genes (99.4%) were similar to sequences of known proteins and could be annotated (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab6">6</a>). The average gene length was 2818.5bp, and the average CDS length was 1082.0bp. The average exon number per gene was 4.2, with an average exon length of 260.5bp and average intron length of 550.8bp (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab5">5</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-5"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab5" data-test="table-caption">Table 5 General statistics for feature of predicted protein-coding genes of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome. Protein-coding genes were predicted through the annotation strategy of de novo prediction and evidence based on homology and transcriptome data. The gene model was integrated with EVM and corrected by PASA to obtain the final set of protein-coding genes</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/5"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
<div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-6"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab6" data-test="table-caption">Table 6 Functional annotation of protein-coding genes against different databases. Gene functions were obtained from the best BLASTP hit</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/6"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">Annotation of non-coding RNA</h3><p>The tRNA genes were discovered with tRNAscan-SE software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Lowe TM, Eddy SR. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 1997;25(5):95564." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1773">57</a>]. The rRNA, miRNA, and snRNA were predicted by INFERNAL software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Nawrocki EP, Kolbe DL, Eddy SR. Infernal 1.0: inference of RNA alignments. Bioinformatics. 2009;25(10):13357." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1776">58</a>] against the Rfam database 9.1 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Griffiths-Jones S, Moxon S, Marshall M, Khanna A, Eddy SR, Bateman A. Rfam: annotating non-coding RNAs in complete genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 2005;33:D1214." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1779">59</a>]. We annotated non-coding RNA and identified 692 tRNAs, 68 rRNAs, 702 snRNAs, and 1376 microRNAs in the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome (Tables<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab4">4</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab7">7</a>). The average lengths of microRNAs, tRNAs, rRNAs, and snRNAs were 124.89bp, 75.27bp, 207.79bp, and 118.21bp, respectively (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab7">7</a>). We deposited the genome sequence in the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="BIG Data Center Members (BDCM). Database resources of the BIG Data Center in. Nucleic. Acids Res. 2019;47(D1):D8D14." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1795">60</a>].
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-7"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab7" data-test="table-caption">Table 7 Identification of non-coding RNAs of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome. The tRNAs were predicted by tRNAscan-SE software. The rRNA, miRNA and snRNA genes were extracted by INFERNAL software against the Rfam database</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/7"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Assessment of genome quality</h3><p>We assessed genome quality using the following methods: Burrow-Wheeler Aligner (BWA), Core Eukaryotic Genes Mapping Approach (CEGMA), and Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs (BUSCO). First, in order to assess the quality of genome assembly, we aligned the high-quality Illumina short reads to the assembly using BWA (<a href="http://bio-bwa.sourceforge.net">http://bio-bwa.sourceforge.net</a>, parameters -o 1 -i 15) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Li H, Durbin R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with burrows-wheeler transform. Bioinformatics. 2009;25(14):175460." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1968">61</a>]. According to BWA method, 87.41% of raw reads were mapped to the genome with 93.34% coverage (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab8">8</a>). Next, we used CEGMA and BUSCO to estimate completeness of the assembly. CEGMA is a set of conserved protein families for a wide range of eukaryotes, and is used to identify exonintron structures of these conserved protein families in a new genomic sequence [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Parra G, Bradnam K, Korf I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in 2007; 23(9):10611067." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1974">62</a>]. CEGMA analysis revealed 223 out of 248 ultraconserved eukaryotic genes (89.9%) in the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome indicating integrity for the core genes in the assembly (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab9">9</a>). Moreover, completeness of the assembly also was assessed using BUSCO [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Simao FA, Waterhouse RM, Ioannidis P, Kriventseva EV, Zdobnov EM. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics. 2015;31(19):32102." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1984">63</a>] combined with TBLASTN [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Altschul SF, Madden TL, Schffer AA, Zhang J, Zhang Z, Miller W, et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 1997;25(17):3389402." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1987">46</a>], Augustus (version 3.0.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Stanke M, Waack S. Gene prediction with a hidden Markov model and a new intron submodel. Bioinformatics. 2003;19(2):ii21525." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1990">40</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Stanke M, Schoffmann O, Morgenstern B, Waack S. Gene prediction in eukaryotes with a generalized hidden Markov model that uses hints from external sources. BMC Bioinform. 2006;7(1):62." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1993">41</a>], and HMMER (version 3.1b2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Mistry J, Finn RD, Eddy SR, Bateman A, Punta M. Challenges in homology search: HMMER3 and convergent evolution of coiled-coil regions. Nucleic Acids Res. 2013;41(12):e121." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d52386e1996">64</a>]. The BUSCO analysis showed that our assemblies contained 86.8% complete and 1.7% fragmented embryophyta orthologs, suggesting that the assembly quality was high (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab10">10</a>).
</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-8"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab8" data-test="table-caption">Table 8 Genome coverage rate of raw data based on the BWA method. Mapping rate was generated by mapping raw reads to the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome to express the reliability of the genome coverage</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/8"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
<div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-9"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab9" data-test="table-caption">Table 9 CEGMA analysis results of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/9"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
<div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-10"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab10" data-test="table-caption">Table 10 BUSCO results of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome. C: Complete BUSCOs; S: Complete and single-copy BUSCOs; D: Complete and duplicated BUSCOs; F: Fragmented BUSCOs; M: Missing BUSCOs; n: Total BUSCO groups searched</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5/tables/10"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Utility and discussion</h3><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec12">Description of database</h4><p>The genome assembly of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> consisted of 14,036 contigs with a total size of 1.095 Gb. Finally, we assembled 2638 scaffolds with a total size of 1.107 Gb, contig N50 of 117kb, and scaffold N50 of 950kb. On the basis of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genomic sequences, we predicted 39,725 protein-coding genes, and identified 692 tRNAs, 68 rRNAs, 702 snRNAs, 1376 microRNAs, and 691Mb transposable elements. We assessed the quality and completeness of the assembled genome through BWA, CEGMA mapping, and BUSCO mapping (Tables<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab8">8</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab9">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#Tab10">10</a>). The results showed that our assembly had high quality. All raw data for genome assembly are deposited at NCBI. The genome sequence is deposited in the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center (<a href="https://bigd.big.ac.cn/gwh">https://bigd.big.ac.cn/gwh</a>) (accession number GWHABHL00000000).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec13">Significance of database</h4><p>Halophytes belong to several families and are distributed among multiple clades; this broad distribution pattern suggests that the salinity tolerance mechanisms of halophytes have evolved numerous times or have multiple origins [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Flowers TJ, Galal HK, Bromham L. Evolution of halophytes: multiple origins of salt tolerance in land plants. Funct Plant Biol. 2010;37(7):60412." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2170">2</a>]. As a result, halophytes not only exhibit a wide range of salinity tolerance but have also evolved diverse molecular and physiological mechanisms for salinity tolerance [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Flowers TJ, Galal HK, Bromham L. Evolution of halophytes: multiple origins of salt tolerance in land plants. Funct Plant Biol. 2010;37(7):60412." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2173">2</a>]. This diversity complicates discovery of the salinity tolerance mechanisms of halophytes. To date, almost all known molecular mechanisms of salinity tolerance were characterized in glycophytes such as rice, wheat, and Arabidopsis [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Flowers TJ, Colmer TD. Salinity tolerance in halophytes. New Phytol. 2008;179(4):94563." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2176">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Munns R, Tester M. Mechanisms of salinity tolerance. Annu Rev Plant Biol. 2008;59(1):65181." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2176_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Flowers TJ. Physiology of halophytes. Plant Soil. 1985;89(13):4156." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2179">6</a>]. Glycophytes only provide limited insights into mechanisms of salinity tolerance, and extreme halophytes may have enormous values for improving our understanding of salinity tolerance mechanisms. The genome sequence of extreme halophytes will unlock their molecular studies in salinity tolerance.</p><p>The Gramineae is an important plant group because it includes many important food crops, such as rice, wheat, maize, and barley. <i>P. tenuiflora</i>, an extreme Gramineae halophyte, is closely related to barley and wheat. Zhang et al. (2013) reported that <i>P. tenuiflora</i> can grow normally for 6days under 900mM NaCl and survive at pH11 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Zhang X, Wei L, Wang Z, Wang T. Physiological and molecular features of Puccinellia tenuiflora tolerating salt and alkaline-salt stress. J Integr Plant Biol. 2013;55(3):26276." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2191">23</a>]. Wang et al. (2006) found that <i>P. tenuiflora</i> survived 670mmol/L NaCl [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Wang X, Sun G, Wang J, Cao W, Liang J, Yu Z, et al. Relationships among MDA content, plasma membrane permeability and the chlorophyll fluorescence parameters of Puccinellia tenuiflora seedlings under NaCl stress. Acta Ecol Sin. 2006;26(1):1229." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2197">13</a>]. A growing number of molecular biology studies have focused on this species owing to its strong salinity tolerance and high genetic value for cereal improvement [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang YC, Yang CP, Liu GF, Jiang J. Development of a cDNA microarray to identify gene expression of Puccinellia tenuiflora under saline-alkali stress. Plant Physiol Biochem. 2007;45(8):56776." href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang Y, Chu Y, Liu G, Wang MH, Jiang J, Hou Y, et al. Identification of expressed sequence tags in an alkali grass (Puccinellia tenuiflora) cDNA library. J Plant Physiol. 2007;164(1):7889." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu H, Zhang XX, Takano T, Liu SK. Characterization of a PutCAX1 gene from Puccinellia tenuiflora that confers Ca2+ and Ba2+ tolerance in yeast. Biochem Biophys Res Commun. 2009;383(4):3926." href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_2">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Xie L, Takahashi R, Liu SK, Takano T. Cloning of a high-affinity K+ transporter gene PutHKT2;1 from Puccinellia tenuiflora and its functional comparison with OsHKT2; 1 from rice in yeast and Arabidopsis. J Exp Bot. 2009;60(12):3491502." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_3">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Liu SK, Takano T. Expression of the AKT1-type K+ channel gene from Puccinellia tenuiflora, PutAKT1, enhances salt tolerance in Arabidopsis. Plant Cell Rep. 2010;29(8):86574." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_4">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ardie SW, Nishiuchi S, Liu SK, Takano T. Ectopic expression of the channel  subunits from Puccinellia tenuiflora (KPutB1) and rice (KOB1) alters K+/Na+ homeostasis of yeast and Arabidopsis. Mol Biotechnol. 2011;48(1):7686." href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_5">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yu JJ, Chen SX, Zhao Q, Wang T, Yang CP, Diaz C, et al. Physiological and proteomic analysis of salinity tolerance in Puccinellia tenuiflora. J Proteome Res. 2011;10(9):385270." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_6">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang X, Wei L, Wang Z, Wang T. Physiological and molecular features of Puccinellia tenuiflora tolerating salt and alkaline-salt stress. J Integr Plant Biol. 2013;55(3):26276." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_7">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yu JJ, Chen SX, Wang T, Sun GR, Dai SJ. Comparative proteomic analysis of Puccinellia tenuiflora leaves under Na2CO3 stress. Int J Mol Sci. 2013;14(1):174062." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_8">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang P, Cui YN, Gao L, Wang SM. Construction of RNAi expression vector of CYP86A gene in halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora. Acta Pratacul Sin. 2017;26(6):10510." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_9">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang WD, Wang P, Bao Z, Ma Q, Duan LJ, Bao AK, et al. SOS1, HKT1;5, and NHX1 synergistically modulate Na+ homeostasis in the halophytic grass Puccinellia tenuiflora. Front Plant Sci. 2017;8:576." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_10">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ye X, Wang H, Cao X, Jin X, Cui F, Bu Y, et al. Transcriptome profiling of Puccinellia tenuiflora during seed germination under a long-term saline-alkali stress. BMC Genomics. 2019;20(1):589." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2201_11">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Yin Z, Zhang H, Zhao Q, Yoo M-J, Zhu N, Yu J, et al. Physiological and comparative proteomic analyses of saline-alkali NaHCO3-responses in leaves of halophyte Puccinellia tenuiflora. Plant Soil. 2019;437(12):13758." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2204">28</a>]. In the present study, we sequenced and assembled the <i>P. tenuiflora</i> genome (2n=14, size 1.107 Gb). Our work may improve current understanding of salinity tolerance and provides genetic resources for cereal improvement.</p></div></div></section>
                    <section aria-labelledby="availability-of-data-and-materials" data-title="Availability of data and materials"><div class="c-article-section" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="availability-of-data-and-materials">Availability of data and materials</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-content">
              
              <p>All raw data of genome sequencing are available at NCBI. Accession numbers for raw data of genome assembly are SRR7503009-SRR7503032, and SRP152905 and SRP239345 for transcriptional data. The genome sequence was deposited in the Genome Warehouse in National Genomics Data Center (<a href="https://bigd.big.ac.cn/gwh">https://bigd.big.ac.cn/gwh</a>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="BIG Data Center Members (BDCM). Database resources of the BIG Data Center in. Nucleic. Acids Res. 2019;47(D1):D8D14." href="/articles/10.1186/s12864-020-6727-5#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d52386e2257">60</a>], Beijing Institute of Genomics (BIG), Chinese Academy of Sciences, under accession number GWHABHL00000000 that is publicly accessible at <a href="https://bigd.big.ac.cn/search?dbId=gwh&amp;q=GWHABHL00000000&amp;page=1">https://bigd.big.ac.cn/search?dbId=gwh&amp;q=GWHABHL00000000&amp;page=1</a>. Seeds of <i>P. tenuiflora</i> is available from the corresponsing author upon request.</p>
